Go through the entire data analysis process, starting by posing a question and finishing by sharing your findings.&l;/p&g;\n\n&l;p&g;Prepare for this project with: &l;a href=\&q;https://www.udacity.com/course/viewer#!/c-ud170\&q;&g;Intro to Data Analysis&l;/a&g;&l;/p&g;\n\n&l;p&g;&l;strong&g;Wrangle OpenStreetMap Data&l;/strong&g;&l;br&g;&l;br&g;\nChoose any area of the world in &l;a href=\&q;https://www.openstreetmap.org\&q; target=\&q;_blank\&q;&g;OpenStreetMap &l;/a&g; and use data munging techniques, such as assessing the quality of the data for validity, accuracy, completeness, consistency and uniformity, &l;br&g;\nto clean the OpenStreetMap data for a part of the world that you care about. Choose between MongoDB or SQL as the data schema to complete your project. &l;/p&g;\n\n&l;p&g;&l;strong&g;Explore, Summarize, and Discover Interesting Insights from Datasets&l;/strong&g;&l;br&g;&l;br&g;\nUse R to apply exploratory data analysis techniques. Practice understanding a single variable and relationships between multiple variables, and explore a selected data set for distributions, outliers, and anomalies.&l;/p&g;\n\n&l;p&g;Prepare for this project with: &l;a href=\&q;https://www.udacity.com/course/viewer#!/c-ud651\&q;&g;Data Analysis with R&l;/a&g;&l;/p&g;\n\n&l;p&g;&l;strong&g;Identify Fraud from the Enron Email Dataset&l;/strong&g;&l;br&g;&l;br&g;\nPlay detective and put your machine learning skills to use by building an algorithm to identify Enron Employees who may have committed fraud based on the public Enron financial and email dataset. &l;/p&g;\n\n&l;p&g;Prepare for this project with:  &l;a href=\&q;https://www.udacity.com/course/viewer#!/c-ud120\&q;&g;Intro to Machine Learning&l;/a&g;&l;/p&g;\n\n&l;p&g;&l;strong&g;Tell Stories with Data Visualization&l;/strong&g;&l;br&g;&l;br&g;\nCreate a data visualization from a data set that tells a story or highlights patterns in the data. Your work will be a reflection of the theory and best practices of data visualization.&l;/p&g;\n\n&l;p&g;Prepare for this project with:  &l;a href=\&q;https://www.udacity.com/course/viewer#!/c-ud507\&q;&g;Data Visualization&l;/a&g;&l;/p&g;\n\n&l;p&g;&l;strong&g;Design and Analyze an A/B Test&l;/strong&g;&l;/p&g;\n\n&l;p&g;Make design decisions for an A/B test, including which metrics to measure and how long the test should be run. You will also complete a capstone project in your chosen domain.&q;,&q;slug&q;:&q;machine-learning-engineer-nanodegree--nd009&q;,&q;starter&q;:false,&q;student_groups&q;:[&q;5783912581955584&q;,&q;5807803480145920&q;,&q;5270207414927360&q;,&q;4690496762675200&q;,&q;5081227872436224&q;,&q;5319291655946240&q;,&q;6066628850352128&q;,&q;5590634796417024&q;,&q;5005136415686656&q;,&q;6095420591439872&q;,&q;5400542882562048&q;,&q;5871573019656192&q;,&q;6065194831446016&q;,&q;5583925651701760&q;,&q;5008831690833920&q;,&q;6182998238822400&q;,&q;5398639458123776&q;,&q;6193470669324288&q;,&q;5509474824224768&q;,&q;4844724079558656&q;,&q;5144523752341504&q;,&q;6515371784536064&q;,&q;6217236604518400&q;,&q;5527193434980352&q;,&q;5975056925327360&q;,&q;6216342131441664&q;,&q;5345768759361536&q;,&q;bd-nd009-students&q;],&q;subtitle&q;:&q;Supervised Learning, Unsupervised Learning, Reinforcement Learning, and Deep Learning.&q;,&q;summary&q;:&q;In this program you will master Supervised, Unsupervised, Reinforcement, and Deep Learning fundamentals. You will also complete a capstone project in your chosen domain.&q;,&q;syllabus&q;:&q;&l;p&g;As a student in the Machine Learning Nanodegree program, you will build the  projects listed below. Each project has a &l;strong&g;supporting course&l;/strong&g;. Reviewers will provide feedback on your projects and guidance on how to take your project to the next level.&l;/p&g;\n\n&l;p&g;&l;em&g;Note: Unless otherwise mentioned in the individual project descriptions, you will need to implement your projects in *&l;/em&g;Python 2.7&l;strong&g;. Familiarity with numerical and scientific computing libraries like **NumPy&l;/strong&g; and &l;strong&g;SciPy&l;/strong&g; will be very helpful.*&l;/p&g;\n\n&l;h3&g;Project 0: Titanic Survival Exploration (Optional)&l;/h3&g;\n\n&l;p&g;In this project, you will create decision functions that attempt to predict survival outcomes from the 1912 Titanic disaster based on each passenger’s features, such as sex and age. You will start with a simple algorithm and increase its complexity until you are able to accurately predict the outcomes for at least 80% of the passengers in the provided data. This project will introduce you to some of the concepts of machine learning as you start the Nanodegree program.&l;/p&g;\n\n&l;p&g;&l;strong&g;&l;em&g;The supporting course covers:&l;/em&g;&l;/strong&g; Introduction to Artificial Intelligence and Machine Learning.&l;/p&g;\n\n&l;h3&g;Project 1: Predicting Boston Housing Prices&l;/h3&g;\n\n&l;p&g;You want to be the best real estate agent out there. In order to compete with other agents in your area, you decide to use machine learning. You are going to use various statistical analysis tools to build the best model to predict the value of a given house. Your task is to find the best price your client can sell their house at. The best guess from a model is one that best generalizes the data.&l;/p&g;\n\n&l;p&g;&l;strong&g;&l;em&g;The supporting course covers:&l;/em&g;&l;/strong&g;  Statistics Review &a;amp; Supporting Libraries, Evaluating Model Performance, Model Evaluation &a;amp; Validation, and Model Optimization.&l;/p&g;\n\n&l;h3&g;Project 2: Finding Donors for CharityML&l;/h3&g;\n\n&l;p&g;CharityML, a fictitious charity organization, has brought you on board to help build an algorithm to best identify potential donors and reduce overhead cost of sending mail. Your goal will be evaluate and optimize several different supervised learners to determine which algorithm will provide the highest donation yield while also reducing the total number of letters being sent.&l;/p&g;\n\n&l;p&g;&l;strong&g;&l;em&g;The supporting course covers:&l;/em&g;&l;/strong&g;  Supervised Learning Intro, Decision Trees, Regression, Neural Networks, Kernel Methods, Instance Based Learning, Bayesian Learning, Ensemble Learning.&l;/p&g;\n\n&l;h3&g;Project 3: Creating Customer Segments&l;/h3&g;\n\n&l;p&g;A wholesale distributor is looking to optimize their delivery methods, and has reached out to you for help. In this project, you will be given unstructured data about the customers. You will then use unsupervised learning techniques to find similarities between them, segment them into distinct categories, and finally recommend the best delivery service for each cluster of customers.&l;/p&g;\n\n&l;p&g;&l;strong&g;&l;em&g;The supporting course covers:&l;/em&g;&l;/strong&g;   Clustering, Feature Scaling, Feature Selection, Feature Transformation, Semi-Supervised Learning.&l;/p&g;\n\n&l;h3&g;Project 4: Train a Smartcab to Drive&l;/h3&g;\n\n&l;p&g;A smartcab is a self-driving car from the not-so-distant future that ferries people from one arbitrary location to another. In this project, you will use reinforcement learning to train a smartcab how to drive in real-time, optimizing for both safety and efficiency.&l;/p&g;\n\n&l;p&g;&l;strong&g;&l;em&g;The supporting course covers:&l;/em&g;&l;/strong&g;  Markov Decision Processes, Reinforcement Learning, and Game Theory.&l;/p&g;\n\n&l;h3&g;Project 5: Build a Digit Recognition Program&l;/h3&g;\n\n&l;p&g;In this project, you will create a live camera application or program that prints numbers it observes in real time from images it is given, using what you&a;#39;ve learned about deep neural networks and convolutional neural networks.&l;/p&g;\n\n&l;p&g;&l;strong&g;&l;em&g;The supporting course covers:&l;/em&g;&l;/strong&g;  Deep Neural Networks, Convolutional Neural Networks.&l;/p&g;\n\n&l;h3&g;Project 6: Capstone Project&l;/h3&g;\n\n&l;p&g;In this capstone project, you will leverage what you’ve learned throughout the Nanodegree program to solve a problem of your choice by applying machine learning algorithms and techniques. You will first &l;strong&g;define&l;/strong&g; the problem you want to solve and investigate potential solutions and performance metrics. Next, you will &l;strong&g;analyze&l;/strong&g; the problem through visualizations and data exploration to have a better understanding of what algorithms and features are appropriate for solving it. You will then &l;strong&g;implement&l;/strong&g; your algorithms and metrics of choice, documenting the preprocessing, refinement, and postprocessing steps along the way. Afterwards, you will collect &l;strong&g;results&l;/strong&g; about the performance of the models used, visualize significant quantities, and validate/justify these values. Finally, you will construct &l;strong&g;conclusions&l;/strong&g; about your results, and discuss whether your implementation adequately solves the problem. With your new social network, you can explore relationships and gain insight into how you fit into your own social networks.&l;/p&g;&q;,&q;faq&q;:&q;### When does the course begin? This class is self paced. You can begin whenever you like and then follow your own pace. It’s a good idea to set goals for yourself to make sure you stick with the course.### How long will the course be available?This class will always be available! ### How do I know if this course is for me? Take a look at the \&q;Class Summary,\&q; \&q;What Should I Know,\&q; and \&q;What Will I Learn\&q; sections above. If you want to know more, just enroll in the course and start exploring.### Can I skip individual videos? What about entire lessons? Yes! The point is for you to learn what YOU need (or want) to learn. If you already know something, feel free to skip ahead. If you ever find that you’re confused, you can always go back and watch something that you skipped.### What are the rules on collaboration? Collaboration is a great way to learn. You should do it! The key is to use collaboration as a way to enhance learning, not as a way of sharing answers without understanding them. ### Why are there so many questions? Udacity classes are a little different from traditional courses. We intersperse our video segments with interactive questions. There are many reasons for including these questions: to get you thinking, to check your understanding, for fun, etc... But really, they are there to help you learn. They are NOT there to evaluate your intelligence, so try not to let them stress you out.### What should I do while I’m watching the videos? Learn actively! testing, or split testing, is used by companies like Google, Microsoft, Amazon, Ebay/Paypal, Netflix, and numerous others to decide which changes are worth launching. By using A/B tests to make decisions, you can base your decisions on actual data, rather than relying on intuition or HiPPO&a;#39;s - the highest paid person&a;#39;s opinion! Designing good A/B tests and drawing valid conclusions can be difficult. You can almost never measure exactly what you want to know (such as whether the users are &a;quot;happier&a;quot; on one version of the site), so you need to find good proxies. You need sanity checks to make sure your experimental set-up isn&a;#39;t flawed, and you need to use a variety of statistical techniques to make sure the results you&a;#39;re seeing aren&a;#39;t due to chance. This course will walk you through the entire process. Analyze the results of an A/B test that was run by Udacity and recommend whether or not to launch the change.&l;/p&g;&q;,&q;image&q;:&q;&q;,&q;index&q;:&q;&q;,&q;name&q;:&q;Design an A/B Test&q;,&q;short_summary&q;:&q;&q;,&q;supporting_courses&q;:null}],&q;related_degree_keys&q;:[],&q;required_knowledge&q;:&q;&l;p&g;This course requires introductory knowledge of descriptive and inferential statistics. If you haven&a;#39;t learned these topics, or need a refresher, they are covered in the Udacity courses &l;a href=\&q;https://www.udacity.com/course/intro-to-descriptive-statistics--ud827\&q; target=\&q;_blank\&q;&g;Inferential Statistics&l;/a&g; and &l;a href=\&q;https://www.udacity.com/course/intro-to-descriptive-statistics--ud827\&q; target=\&q;_blank\&q;&g;Descriptive Statistics&l;/a&g;.&l;/p&g;&l;p&g;Prior experience with A/B testing is not required, and neither is programming knowledge.&l;/p&g;&q;,&q;seo_keywords&q;:&q;&q;,&q;selling_points&q;:{&q;images_url&q;:null,&q;selling_keys&q;:null},&q;short_summary&q;:&q;Design and implement an A/B test to determine the efficacy of potential improvements to an online site or mobile app while specifying metrics to measure.&q;,&q;slug&q;:&q;ab-testing--ud257&q;,&q;starter&q;:false,&q;student_groups&q;:[],&q;subtitle&q;:&q;Online Experiment Design and Analysis&q;,&q;summary&q;:&q;&l;p&g;This course will cover the design and analysis of A/B tests, also known as split tests, which are online experiments used to test potential improvements to a website or mobile application. Two versions of the website are shown to different users - usually the existing website and a potential change. Then, the results are analyzed to determine whether the change is an improvement worth launching. This course will cover how to choose and characterize metrics to evaluate your experiments, how to design an experiment with enough statistical power, how to analyze the results and draw valid conclusions, and how to ensure that the the participants of your experiments are adequately protected.&l;/p&g;&q;,&q;syllabus&q;:&q;&l;h3&g;Lesson 1: Overview of A/B Testing&l;/h3&g;&l;p&g;This lesson will cover what A/B testing is and what it can be used for. It will also cover an example A/B test from start to finish, including how to decide how long to run the experiment, how to construct a binomial confidence interval for the results, and how to decide whether the change is worth the launch cost.&l;/p&g;&l;h3&g;Lesson 2: Policy and Ethics for Experiments&l;/h3&g;&l;p&g;This lesson will cover how to make sure the participants of your experiments are adequately protected and what questions you should be asking regarding the ethicality of experiments. It will cover four main ethics principles to consider when designing experiments: the risk to the user, the potential benefits, what alternatives users have to participating in the experiment, and the sensitivity of the data being collected.&l;/p&g;&l;h3&g;Lesson 3: Choosing and Characterizing Metrics&l;/h3&g;&l;p&g;One of the most important and time-consuming pieces of designing an A/B test is choosing and validating metrics to use in evaluating your experiment. This lesson will cover techniques for brainstorming metrics, what to do when you can&a;#39;t measure what you want directly, and characteristics you should consider when validating your metrics.&l;/p&g;&l;h3&g;Lesson 4: Designing an Experiment&l;/h3&g;&l;p&g;This lesson will cover how to design an A/B test. This includes how to choose which users will be in your experiment and control group - different online definitions of a &a;quot;user&a;quot;, and what effects different choices will have on your experiment. It will also cover when to  limit your experiment to a subset of your entire user base, how to calculate how many events you will need in order to draw strong conclusions from your results, and how this translates into how long to run the experiment. Finally, the lesson will cover how various design decisions affect the size of your experiment, so you will know which decisions to revisit if you need results more quickly.&l;/p&g;&l;h3&g;Lesson 5: Analyzing Results&l;/h3&g;&l;p&g;This lesson will cover how to analyze the results of your experiments. Step one is always to run some sanity checks so that you can catch problems with your experiment set-up. Then, you will learn how to check conclusions with multiple methods, including a hypothesis test on the effect size and a binomial sign test, if you get results that surprise you. You will also learn how measuring multiple metrics for the same experiment can make analysis difficult, and some techniques for handling multiple metrics. Finally, you will learn about several analysis &a;quot;gotchas&a;quot;, and what to do if you see them, including how Simpson&a;#39;s Paradox can affect A/B tests, and why even statistically significant results might disappear when you launch.&l;/p&g;&l;h3&g;Final Project: Design and Analyze an A/B Test&l;/h3&g;&l;p&g;Make design decisions for an A/B test, including which metrics to measure and how long the test should be run. If you need a refresher on any of these topics, you can check out these courses:&l;/p&g;&l;ul&g;&l;li&g;&l;p&g;&l;a href=\&q;https://www.udacity.com/course/intro-to-computer-science--cs101\&q;&g;Intro to Computer Science&l;/a&g; (You should know basic data structures and control statements, and be able to write and import functions.)&l;/p&g;&l;/li&g;&l;li&g;&l;p&g;&l;a href=\&q;https://www.udacity.com/course/intro-to-inferential-statistics--ud201\&q;&g;Inferential Statistics&l;/a&g;&l;/p&g;&l;/li&g;&l;li&g;&l;p&g;&l;a href=\&q;https://www.udacity.com/course/intro-to-descriptive-statistics--ud827\&q;&g;Descriptive Statistics&l;/a&g;&l;/p&g;&l;/li&g;&l;/ul&g;&l;p&g;One additional course that would be nice to have is Intro to &l;a href=\&q;https://www.udacity.com/course/intro-to-data-science--ud359\&q;&g;Data Science&l;/a&g;, as this will get you familiar with scientific problem-solving.  However, completion of that class isn&a;#39;t required for success.  We will also use a tiny bit of &l;a href=\&q;https://www.udacity.com/course/how-to-use-git-and-github--ud775\&q;&g;git&l;/a&g;, which you can also learn about on Udacity.&l;/p&g;&l;p&g;One thing that we don’t require is previous exposure to machine learning.  If you’re a machine learning beginner, you’re in the right place.&l;/p&g;&q;,&q;seo_keywords&q;:&q;&q;,&q;selling_points&q;:{&q;images_url&q;:null,&q;selling_keys&q;:null},&q;short_summary&q;:&q;This class will teach you the end-to-end process of investigating data through a machine learning lens, and you&s;ll apply what you&s;ve learned to a real-world data set.&q;,&q;slug&q;:&q;intro-to-machine-learning--ud120&q;,&q;starter&q;:false,&q;student_groups&q;:[&q;5699377246502912&q;,&q;6737379171237888&q;,&q;6542316789039104&q;],&q;subtitle&q;:&q;Pattern Recognition for Fun and Profit&q;,&q;summary&q;:&q;&l;p&g;Machine Learning is a first-class ticket to the most exciting careers in data analysis today. As data sources proliferate along with the computing power to process them, going straight to the data is one of the most straightforward ways to quickly gain insights and make predictions.  &l;/p&g;&l;p&g;Machine learning brings together computer science and statistics to harness that predictive power. It’s a must-have skill for all aspiring data analysts and data scientists, or anyone else who wants to wrestle all that raw data into refined trends and predictions.&l;/p&g;&l;p&g;This is a class that will teach you the end-to-end process of investigating data through a machine learning lens. It will teach you how to extract and identify useful features that best represent your data, a few of the most important machine learning algorithms, and how to evaluate the performance of your machine learning algorithms.&l;/p&g;&l;p&g;This course is also a part of our &l;a href=\&q;https://www.udacity.com/course/data-analyst-nanodegree--nd002\&q;&g;Data Analyst&l;/a&g; Nanodegree.&l;/p&g;&q;,&q;syllabus&q;:&q;&l;p&g;You’ll learn how to start with a question and/or a dataset, and use machine learning to turn them into insights. &l;/p&g;&l;h3&g;Lessons 1-4: Supervised Classification&l;/h3&g;&l;p&g;&l;strong&g;Naive Bayes:&l;/strong&g; We jump in headfirst, learning perhaps the world’s greatest algorithm for classifying text.&l;/p&g;&l;p&g;&l;strong&g;Support Vector Machines (SVMs):&l;/strong&g; One of the top 10 algorithms in machine learning, and a must-try for many classification tasks.  What makes it special?  The ability to generate new features independently and on the fly.&l;/p&g;&l;p&g;&l;strong&g;Decision Trees:&l;/strong&g; Extremely straightforward, often just as accurate as an SVM but (usually) way faster.  The launch point for more sophisticated methods, like random forests and boosting.&l;/p&g;&l;h3&g;Lesson 5: Datasets and Questions&l;/h3&g;&l;p&g;Behind any great machine learning project is a great dataset that the algorithm can learn from.  We were inspired by a treasure trove of email and financial data from the Enron corporation, which would normally be strictly confidential but became public when the company went bankrupt in a blizzard of fraud.  Follow our lead as we wrestle this dataset into a machine-learning-ready format, in anticipation of trying to predict cases of fraud.&l;/p&g;&l;h3&g;Lesson 6 and 7: Regressions and Outliers&l;/h3&g;&l;p&g;Regressions are some of the most widely used machine learning algorithms, and rightly share prominence with classification.  What’s a fast way to make mistakes in regression, though?  Have troublesome outliers in your data.  We’ll tackle how to identify and clean away those pesky data points.&l;/p&g;&l;h3&g;Lesson 8: Unsupervised Learning&l;/h3&g;&l;p&g;&l;strong&g;K-Means Clustering:&l;/strong&g; The flagship algorithm when you don’t have labeled data to work with, and a quick method for pattern-searching when approaching a dataset for the first time.&l;/p&g;&l;h3&g;Lessons 9-12: Features, Features, Features&l;/h3&g;&l;p&g;&l;strong&g;Feature Creation:&l;/strong&g; Taking your human intuition about the world and turning it into data that a computer can use.&l;/p&g;&l;p&g;&l;strong&g;Feature Selection:&l;/strong&g; Einstein said it best: make everything as simple as possible, and no simpler.  In this case, that means identifying the most important features of your data.&l;/p&g;&l;p&g;&l;strong&g;Principal Component Analysis:&l;/strong&g; A more sophisticated take on feature selection, and one of the crown jewels of unsupervised learning.&l;/p&g;&l;p&g;&l;strong&g;Feature Scaling:&l;/strong&g; Simple tricks for making sure your data and your algorithm play nicely together.&l;br&g;Learning from Text: More information is in text than any other format, and there are some effective but simple tools for extracting that information.&l;/p&g;&l;h3&g;Lessons 13-14: Validation and Evaluation&l;/h3&g;&l;p&g;&l;strong&g;Training/testing data split:&l;/strong&g; How do you know that what you’re doing is working?  You don’t, unless you validate.  The train-test split is simple to do, and the gold standard for understanding your results.&l;/p&g;&l;p&g;&l;strong&g;Cross-validation:&l;/strong&g; Take the training/testing split and put it on steroids.  Validate your machine learning results like a pro.&l;/p&g;&l;p&g;&l;strong&g;Precision, recall, and F1 score:&l;/strong&g;  After all this data-driven work, quantify your results with metrics tailored to what is most important to you.&l;/p&g;&l;h3&g;Lesson 15: Wrapping it all Up&l;/h3&g;&l;p&g;We take a step back and review what we’ve learned, and how it all fits together.  &l;/p&g;&l;h3&g;Projects&l;/h3&g;&l;p&g;Mini-project at the end of each lesson&l;/p&g;&l;p&g;&l;strong&g;Final project:&l;/strong&g; searching for signs of corporate fraud in Enron data&l;/p&g;&q;,&q;tags&q;:[],&q;teaser_video&q;:{&q;transcodings&q;:{&q;480p_1000kbps_mp4&q;:{},&q;480p_mp4&q;:{},&q;480p_ogg&q;:{},&q;720p_mp4&q;:{}}},&q;title&q;:&q;Intro to Machine Learning&q;,&q;tracks&q;:[&q;All&q;,&q;Data Science&q;,&q;Machine Learning&q;],&q;why_nd_summary&q;:&q;&q;,&q;why_nd_data&q;:&q;&q;},{&q;affiliates&q;:[{&q;image&q;:&q;https://lh3.ggpht.com/q4HzkHOhhHjpC2TUGyz6nq3p0ZQbjscdEvTBBx3xMC9kiX7Iq1GOJIIi9K3yRwGw4nXFyOsyW6IeqtaQBdg=s0#w=520&a;h=240&q;,&q;key&q;:&q;zipfian&q;,&q;name&q;:&q;Zipfian&q;}],&q;apply_required&q;:false,&q;available&q;:true,&q;banner_image&q;:&q;https://lh4.ggpht.com/U6QogkXo7B-Tll6-h9dTYVtkBVv_POuKORlwQ3B0T003rUnUGMAQscN6VAoBqwdDAcPjqosCjTqXMvi60YiA=s0#w=1170&a;h=242&q;,&q;capped&q;:true,&q;enables_profiles&q;:false,&q;expected_duration&q;:7,&q;expected_duration_high&q;:0,&q;expected_duration_low&q;:7,&q;expected_duration_unit&q;:&q;weeks&q;,&q;expected_learning&q;:&q;&l;p&g;Learn by doing! You should also be able to describe concepts like functions and objects. Our &l;a href=\&q;https://www.udacity.com/course/intro-to-computer-science--cs101\&q; target=\&q;_blank\&q;&g;Intro to Computer Science&l;/a&g; and &l;a href=\&q;https://www.udacity.com/course/programming-foundations-with-python--ud036\&q; target=\&q;_blank\&q;&g;Programming Fundamentals with Python&l;/a&g; courses are great places to get started.&l;/p&g;&l;p&g;Basic knowledge of HTML and CSS (structuring and styling a web page) is not required but highly recommended. The visualization library, dimple.js, is easier to use than d3.js and requires less background knowledge. Furthermore, a graphic can be created in considerably fewer lines of code using dimple.js as opposed to d3.js.&l;/p&g;&l;p&g;So why should you learn d3.js?&l;/p&g;&l;p&g;Data Driven Documents (d3.js) allows you to build highly customized graphics. If you would like to gain more technical skills and learn more about Javascript and open web standards, then you should complete Lesson 3 and Lesson 4 in order to prepare for the final project.&l;/p&g;&l;p&g;If you would like to complete the final project using d3.js, you should have some experience reading and using documentation. For example, you should be able to code a &l;code&g;for&l;/code&g; loop in Javascript or be able to look up the syntax to work with strings and arrays in Javascript. We recommend taking the &l;a href=\&q;https://www.udacity.com/course/intro-to-javascript--ud803\&q; target=\&q;_blank\&q;&g;Javascript Basics&l;/a&g; course if you have little to no experience with Javascript.&l;/p&g;&q;,&q;seo_keywords&q;:&q;&q;,&q;selling_points&q;:{&q;images_url&q;:null,&q;selling_keys&q;:null},&q;short_summary&q;:&q;Learn the fundamentals of data visualization and apply design and narrative concepts to create your own visualization.&q;,&q;slug&q;:&q;data-visualization-and-d3js--ud507&q;,&q;starter&q;:false,&q;student_groups&q;:[&q;6532249318588416&q;,&q;6039017556017152&q;,&q;bd-ud507-students&q;],&q;subtitle&q;:&q;Communicating with Data&q;,&q;summary&q;:&q;&l;p&g;Learn the fundamentals of data visualization and practice communicating with data. This course covers how to apply design principles, human perception, color theory, and effective storytelling to data visualization. If you present data to others, aspire to be an analyst or data scientist, or if you’d like to become more technical with visualization tools, then you can grow your skills with this course.&l;/p&g;&l;p&g;The course does not cover exploratory approaches to discover insights about data. Instead, the course focuses on how to visually encode and present data to an audience once an insight has been found.&l;/p&g;&l;p&g;This course is part of the &l;a href=\&q;https://www.udacity.com/course/data-analyst-nanodegree--nd002&l;br&g;\&q; target=\&q;_blank\&q;&g;Data Analyst Nanodegree&l;/a&g;.&l;/p&g;&q;,&q;syllabus&q;:&q;&l;h3&g;Lesson 1a Visualization Fundamentals (2 hours)&l;/h3&g;&l;p&g;Learn about the elements of great data visualization. In this lesson, you will meet data visualization experts, learn about data visualization in the context of data science, and learn how to represent data values in visual form.&l;/p&g;&l;h3&g;Lesson 1b D3 Building Blocks (4 hours)&l;/h3&g;&l;p&g;Learn how to use the open standards of the web to create graphical elements. You’ll learn how to select elements on the page, add SVG elements, and how to style SVG elements. Make use of all the Instructor Notes throughout this lesson if you have little to no experience with HTML and CSS.&l;/p&g;&l;h3&g;Mini-Project 1: RAW Visualization (2 hours)&l;/h3&g;&l;p&g;Create a data visualization using a software of your choice. We will provide recommendations for visualization software as well as data sets. We want you to get right into making data visualization so here’s your first chance!&l;/p&g;&l;h3&g;Lesson 2a Design Principles (2 hours)&l;/h3&g;&l;p&g;Which chart type should I use for my data? Which colors should I avoid when making graphics? How do I know if my graphic is effective? Investigate these questions, and learn about the World Cup data set which will be use throughout the rest of the course.&l;/p&g;&l;h3&g;Lesson 2b Dimple.js (4 hours)&l;/h3&g;&l;p&g;Learn how to create graphics using the Dimple JavaScript library. You will learn about this library as a gentle coding introduction before learning about D3.js. You will be able to produce great graphics with minimal code, and all of your graphics will come with interactivity without any extra effort on your part. Dimple, it&a;#39;s simple!&l;/p&g;&l;h3&g;Mini-Project 2: Take Two (2-5 hours)&l;/h3&g;&l;p&g;Find an existing data visualization, critique it for what it does well and what it doesn’t do well, and finally, recreate the graphic using a software tool of your choice. We recommend using Dimple.js, which is covered in Lesson 2b, but we don’t want you to feel constrained by the choice of tools. Use any tool that works for you.&l;/p&g;&l;h3&g;Special Note&l;/h3&g;&l;p&g;At this point in the course, you can start the final project. The remaining content of the course covers narrative structures, types of bias, and maps. All of the code  in Lesson 3 and Lesson 4 pertains to d3.js. If you&a;#39;d like to learn d3.js and complete the final project using d3.js, then please continue. If you prefer to stop, you can complete the final project using dimple.js.&l;/p&g;&l;h3&g;Lesson 3 Narratives (5 hours)&l;/h3&g;&l;p&g;Learn how to incorporate different narrative structures into your visualizations and code along with Jonathan as you create a graphic for the World Cup data set. You’ll learn about different types of bias in the data visualization process and learn how to add context to your data visualizations. By the end of this lesson, you’ll have a solid foundation in D3.js.&l;/p&g;&l;h3&g;Lesson 4 Animation and Interaction (5 hours)&l;/h3&g;&l;p&g;Static graphics are great, but interactive graphics can be even better. Learn how to leverage animation and interaction to bring more data insights to your audience. Code along with Jonathan once again as you learn how to create a bubble map for the World Cup data set.&l;/p&g;&l;h3&g;Final Project: Making an Effective Data Visualization (2 hours or more)&l;/h3&g;&l;p&g;You will create a data visualization that conveys a clear message about a data set. You will use dimple.js or d3.js and collect feedback along the way to arrive at a polished product.&l;/p&g;&l;h4&g;&l;b&g;NOTE:&l;/b&g; As a free student, you are welcome to complete the project to showcase your learning; however, only students enrolled in the &l;a href=\&q;https://www.udacity.com/course/nd002\&q; target=\&q;_blank\&q;&g;Data Analyst Nanodegree&l;/a&g; are able to submit the final project for review and certificate.
